<div id="review_395173855" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/395173855" />
    <a title="Neil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4397314-neil"><img alt="Neil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317645308p2/4397314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/395173855?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil" href="/user/show/4397314-neil">Neil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671319724" href="/book/show/1184347.1632">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397314-neil?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397314-neil?shelf=military-fiction">military-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397314-neil?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397314-neil?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer395173855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11362336677750424813">Typically I find myself fairly cynical when it comes to "alternate history" types of fiction - too often an author's personal bias is clearly reflected in their writing, and, instead of exploring potential changes to history in their alternate world, they attempt to forge a history based on the way <i>they</i> think things should have happened, or, decisions <i>they</i> would've made instead.<br/><br/>That said, I find myself absolutely enthralled with the 16xx/Ring of Fire/Assiti Shards series by Eric Flint. The entir</span>
  <span id="freeText11362336677750424813" style="display:none">Typically I find myself fairly cynical when it comes to "alternate history" types of fiction - too often an author's personal bias is clearly reflected in their writing, and, instead of exploring potential changes to history in their alternate world, they attempt to forge a history based on the way <i>they</i> think things should have happened, or, decisions <i>they</i> would've made instead.<br /><br />That said, I find myself absolutely enthralled with the 16xx/Ring of Fire/Assiti Shards series by Eric Flint. The entire concept of a small, West Virginia mining town being transplanted several hundred years into the past, smack into the middle of the 30 Year's War in Central Europe just grabs me.<br /><br />The characters are quite believable, and I think it is this, along with the clear and consistent acknowledgement that, despite being from so far in the future, the Americans are still strangers in a strange land. The technology and "future knowledge" they bring does provide them a distinct advantage - but early on the main characters realize this will not be enough, and that they must forge a new future for themselves and their loved ones. The hard-earned lessons of American history are applied almost immediately when seeking to create a new Constitution and Bill of Rights - up to and including ensuring that the worst parts of our past are avoided as much as possible.<br /><br />The places, times and people are incredibly well researched - far more so than in some novels or series, and in many ways you can gain an appreciation for the history of Central Europe in the 17th Century, despite this being an "alternate" history.<br /><br />5/5 Will Read Again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11362336677750424813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_72839814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72839814" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/282350-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1213995656p2/282350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72839814?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/282350-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/282350-kristi?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/282350-kristi?shelf=fourstars">fourstars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/282350-kristi?shelf=middling">middling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/282350-kristi?shelf=up-til-3am">up-til-3am</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72839814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13833239135458003745">What a very fun book to read! And what a great way to get someone interested in a period of history. Sure, there's the jingoistic "Americuh, **** yeah!" aspect to it, but it's often played for laughs. <br/><br/>The premise of the book is that about a 6 mile radius sphere of a modern day West Virginian small mining town is suddenly scooped out due to an advanced species' temporal negligance and dropped down in the middle of Germany in 1631, about 10 years into the ferociously vicious and bloody Thirty Year</span>
  <span id="freeText13833239135458003745" style="display:none">What a very fun book to read! And what a great way to get someone interested in a period of history. Sure, there's the jingoistic "Americuh, **** yeah!" aspect to it, but it's often played for laughs. <br /><br />The premise of the book is that about a 6 mile radius sphere of a modern day West Virginian small mining town is suddenly scooped out due to an advanced species' temporal negligance and dropped down in the middle of Germany in 1631, about 10 years into the ferociously vicious and bloody Thirty Years War. <br /><br />They were lucky enough to have brought along their power plant and enough doctors and folks who had multiple guns and other knowhow to make them an increasingly important economic and social force of the time. <br /><br />There are lots of hilarious parts, like the Scots' reactions to the "spirited girls" - American style cheerleaders in their cheerleader outfits. And there are also parts that are true to the times, filth, starvation, illness, rape and a deep lack of freedom for the majority of the population.<br /><br />This kept me up long past my bedtime and now I am going to hunt down at least the next sequel to see if it's still as interesting, educational and entertaining as the first. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13833239135458003745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1502056758" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1502056758" />
    <a title="Colleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125315-colleen"><img alt="Colleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478784395p2/1125315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1502056758?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen" href="/user/show/1125315-colleen">Colleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125315-colleen?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125315-colleen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1502056758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2263925174024368586">My brother absolutely loves this book and I've heard of little nothing else for like six months now. Well I FINALLY read it! And really, the cover made my expectations for this book rock bottom, and I've been putting it off now for a couple weeks because the star spangled 1632 above 3 conquistador looking men about to aim on a red pickup truck with an American flag and armed cowboys just didn't whet my interest enough. Then I read the book and realized I was silly: the book is basically this cov</span>
  <span id="freeText2263925174024368586" style="display:none">My brother absolutely loves this book and I've heard of little nothing else for like six months now. Well I FINALLY read it! And really, the cover made my expectations for this book rock bottom, and I've been putting it off now for a couple weeks because the star spangled 1632 above 3 conquistador looking men about to aim on a red pickup truck with an American flag and armed cowboys just didn't whet my interest enough. Then I read the book and realized I was silly: the book is basically this cover and because of this alone is worthy of being read. <br /><br />If you want to read 600 pages of hillbillies riddling with bullets evil inquisitors and rampaging Croats from the 1600s and the exploits of gumcracking cheerleaders, now the most dangerous special forces on the planet, then this is a book for you. And I have to give credit--the action scenes are really well done and I found it a rollicking read. I see there are like 20 more of these books for some reason and I'll probably keep on reading them. <br /><br />It's not a perfect book by any means--the town is extremely lucky. An alien civilization that likes to make "art" out of messing with the time/space continuum creates a piece where a decaying small town in West Virginia gets plucked up and placed smack dab in Germany, right in the middle of marauding mercenaries busy torturing and raping innocent civilians in the 30 Years War. Luckily for this town though, it has a mine, a power plant, TV station, and all the water/sewage/electrical components have made it through the transfer unscathed. Multiple doctors, a dentist, and most importatly of all this book, a wedding coordinator. (What was up with all the romances in this book?)<br /><br /> A big almost unbelievable piece of luck is the citizenry themselves. Normally a small town in WV would be depicted as toothless, meth-crazed racist unemployed layabouts, just waiting for an apocalypse to break out so they can serve their evil sheriff and go on rape/loot sprees, blending in seemlessly with 1600s terrorlands. A twist though! This town is comprised of extremely patriotic, gun toting, mechanical geniuses, so instead they calmly take stock of their situation and decide to reform the United States of America but this time in Germany and try to avert all the horrors of the future. I am not so sure this book could be applied now, in the era of the smart phone (book is 2000), if it ever was back then. But I was able to buy a large portion of this book though and the author even states in his note to the reader that this optimistic tone was an intentional response to how lower class characters are depicted in fiction. Maybe it's all the Eleanor Roosevelt books I've been reading lately, but on a level I buy it too. Roosevelt's experminental New Deal utopia was in WV after all..<br /><br />And while most towns would not take it as calmly as the one in the book, but I think some would for the main fact that the worst town in the US now would be a Power to Be Feared if transported back like 400 years. Nor is this book like militia-ish, if that makes any sense. A large portion of the town are very pro-union miners and one of the main leaders is an extremely liberal feminist (I even liked her portrayal since there has to be someone thinking or acknowledging how to handle the gender issue). The sheriff wasn't corrupt. The big conservative in the book was just a tad grumpy but still best friends with the feminist school teacher. The preacher and the Catholic priest in town are also BFFs. <br /><br />I even bought how quickly everyone who encountered the Americans was taken in. The Americans were doling out showers, bathrobes, ice cream and car rides after all. The author could have shown at least some of the surrounding towns resisting or debating--other than just tales of their "witchcraft" spreading. But if you're a refugee fleeing the complete shittiness of life then, a welcoming town would be a good place to declare sanctuary. I know some people had issues with the casual violence of the book, but I read this book a bit casually and I thought a lot of it was actually justified. If I was sent back in time to 1632, I'd bring a gun and a ton of bullets myself. <br /><br />There isn't much tension in the book in other words. The good guys are all purely good, the bad guys super bad, and are easily mown down. It's a very cheerful and optimistic book and as strange as the cover advertises. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2263925174024368586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1003567144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1003567144" />
    <a title="Sharon Dodge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4707001-sharon-dodge"><img alt="Sharon Dodge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293572592p2/4707001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003567144?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Dodge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Dodge" href="/user/show/4707001-sharon-dodge">Sharon Dodge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003567144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11536102718811468906">I'll say right off the bat that I'm biased here. I've briefly met Eric Flint, and, curmudgeonly older gentleman that he is, I liked him a lot. <br/><br/>But I think there's a lot to like here, regardless. <i>1632</i> is an easy book to like. It has a U.S. town that's thrown back in time and space (by, no less, a small sliver of an alien lifeform's art) to 1632 Germany, where its inhabitants struggle to determine how they're going to survive. The optimism and fortitude shown by the people of Grantville is sometim</span>
  <span id="freeText11536102718811468906" style="display:none">I'll say right off the bat that I'm biased here. I've briefly met Eric Flint, and, curmudgeonly older gentleman that he is, I liked him a lot. <br /><br />But I think there's a lot to like here, regardless. <i>1632</i> is an easy book to like. It has a U.S. town that's thrown back in time and space (by, no less, a small sliver of an alien lifeform's art) to 1632 Germany, where its inhabitants struggle to determine how they're going to survive. The optimism and fortitude shown by the people of Grantville is sometimes more fantastic than the time travel itself - but it's also a welcome experience in a sea of nauseatingly dystopic literature. From day one, the town decides to tell "the whole truth, and nothing but the truth" to anyone who will listen in this era about their time travel and origin, and from there they cautiously work out a temporary council, new constitution, and new way of life. In a movingly altruistic wave of cooperation, a great swathe of coal miners, machinists, chemists, historians and doctors work together in serious thoughtfulness to do what they can to hold together. And hold together they do. <br /><br />Brilliantly, the town decides to go back to old-school steam-engine power, to embrace nineteenth-century technology (still far ahead of the surrounding areas) to keep their electrical power advantage to protect itself in what is essentially a war zone. As a historian and experienced machinist himself (Flint is a fascinating combination - worked on his PhD in history, quit to work for labor rights and did hard manual labor), these are some of the most compelling sections of the book. Perhaps most surprisingly, they adopt a no-compromises approach to maintaining their social identity. This isn't to say they're isolationist; to the contrary. They adopt half the countryside's refugees and farms and militantly defend their religious and physical freedom in an era of no-joke Inquisition and marauding mercenaries. In fact, Flint's characters quickly and wisely point out that it will be very easy to create a second-class citizenry with Americans first, and to avoid it they work hard to integrate with their neighbors and learn from them. <br /><br />As a result of said association, marriages soon spring up like mushrooms, and if I found the romantic sections wanting at times, I still liked the principle of the thing. Flint has brought together a broad swathe of characters, and though, yes, the lead's a white male, he does an excellent job of bringing in a variety of other characters, notably including a key Jewish father and daughter duo and a boisterous, tough-as-nails ex-Marine black doctor as well as a librarian with a radical past. If his characters sometimes don't work as well as I'd like, well, I'll take an imperfect attempt any day over a perfect absence. <br /><br />Although it's hard for me to imagine there wouldn't have been greater angst about whether they'd return or not to their own time and place, and whether or not to interfere with history by sharing information - how will future inventors invent their creations when they are already known? paradox! help! - the complete dismissal of the issue certainly saves time. Because this book is really about the American spirit; it just about bleeds red, white, and blue. It's a love letter to American determination, history, politics, and science, and it was delightful to read someone who believes in the ability to build a better world - no matter where or when you're at.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11536102718811468906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_693375681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/693375681" />
    <a title="Dj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19115189-dj"><img alt="Dj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428218592p2/19115189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/693375681?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dj" href="/user/show/19115189-dj">Dj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer693375681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11396721153673248934">A book somewhat in the vein of Stirling's 'Nantuckt' series. Not as dark, or as detailed it is a fun romp in the messing up of history. In this particular case the history that they are messing with is the 30 years war. It is something along this lines of the Three Musketeers (Protestant Reformation) meets small town West Virginia. Some of the characters are very well done and this does include the historical figures of whom Gustavus Adalphous is one of the most fun. I don't have enough of a bac</span>
  <span id="freeText11396721153673248934" style="display:none">A book somewhat in the vein of Stirling's 'Nantuckt' series. Not as dark, or as detailed it is a fun romp in the messing up of history. In this particular case the history that they are messing with is the 30 years war. It is something along this lines of the Three Musketeers (Protestant Reformation) meets small town West Virginia. Some of the characters are very well done and this does include the historical figures of whom Gustavus Adalphous is one of the most fun. I don't have enough of a background in regards to the Swedish King that made such a large impression during that time, but in the book that gentleman is just about certifiable and causes a great deal of amusement in almost every appearance he makes on the stage of the book. <br /><br />Unlike the Stirling books, this one doesn't go as deeply into the rational behind why some things are done the way they are and sort of hedges on other issues, but since it is a more light hearted approach as well it doesn't cause much dissonance either. Flint, brings a good mix of the plausible with the fantastic to keep from jarring you out of your suspension of belief while still keeping it light enough to be a quick and enjoyable read.<br /><br />After this opening I am going to go on and start taking a look at the rest of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11396721153673248934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3185869626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3522749420347997134">I would have given it 1 star if not for the fact this book has found a niche audience and massive financial success with over 30 sequels. The first book in the series is full of 2 dimensional characters in a pure wish fulfillment story. The lack of any conflict both external and internal that feels real is annoying and really pushes the writing towards the realms of fanfiction (similar to 50 Shades of Grey). However, the series is a financial success providing pure cotton candy reading for fans </span>
  <span id="freeText3522749420347997134" style="display:none">I would have given it 1 star if not for the fact this book has found a niche audience and massive financial success with over 30 sequels. The first book in the series is full of 2 dimensional characters in a pure wish fulfillment story. The lack of any conflict both external and internal that feels real is annoying and really pushes the writing towards the realms of fanfiction (similar to 50 Shades of Grey). However, the series is a financial success providing pure cotton candy reading for fans willing to trade depth for pubescent male fantasy. Expect misogynistic undertones throughout because of this, but if you love American nationalism, guns and the male gaze this book is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3522749420347997134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0JrCz/x9lCmkrbuYxD6VMuCadRY7xn5w88iYPTv+sFad+zZeSAASz8HEI+8kKs5OgfWCK2vRTykv59SSE3t7Mg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m3LIpj5rExhxx7roJx70XfR3nr1ve/VZrgK8w2iJ9gfWEzw3ihaV/hSuIp/HCq8hlRhpgD9sxAByLfBsQAw9Yw==')})
  }
//]]>

Its captain, Lieutenant Commander Matthew Patrick Red<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1402684045532826914\" style=\"display:none\">Pressed into service when World War II breaks out in the Pacific, the USS Walker---a Great-War vintage &quot;four-stacker&quot; destroyer---finds itself in full retreat from pursuit by Japanese battleships. Its captain, Lieutenant Commander Matthew Patrick Reddy, knows that he and his crew are in dire straits. In desperation, he heads Walker into a squall, hoping it will give them cover---and emerges somewhere else.\n\nFamiliar landmarks appear, but the water teems with monstrous, vicious fish. And there appear to be dinosaurs grazing on the plains of Bali. Gradually Matt and his crew must accept the fact that they are in an alternate world---and they are not alone. Humans have not evolved, but two other species have. And they are at war.\n\nWith its steam power and weaponry, the Walker\'s very existence could alter the balance of power. And for Matt and his crew, who have the means to turn a primitive war into a genocidal Armageddon, one thing becomes clear: They must decide whose side they\'re on. The Ottoman Empire has captured Vienna and is now laying siege to the Austrian government-in-exile established in the city of Linz. Both the United States of Europe and the Kingdom of Bohemia have come to Austria’s assistance, but everyone knows this is going to be a long and brutal struggle.  In order to relieve the pressure on the Austrians, General Mike Stearns proposes to open a second front in the Levant. The USE’s emperor Gustavus Adolphus gives his approval to the plan, and Mike sets it in motion, with the very capable assistance of his wife Rebecca Abrabanel, now the USE’s Secretary of State.  Meanwhile, Poland is coming to a boil. Gretchen Richter, the newly elected chancellor of Saxony, has seized control of Lower Silesia. Her small army is now approached to form an alliance with the Polish revolutionaries who have seized power in the Ruthenian province of Galicia—which, in the universe the time-displaced Americans of Grantville came from, would have constituted the western Ukraine.  Now, the Bohemians send an army led by Morris Roth into Poland, ostensibly to aid the revolutionaries but also with the goal of expanding King Albrecht Wallenstein’s growing empire in eastern Europe. And—the icing on the cake—Mike Stearns sends the Hangman Regiment of his Third Division under the command of Jeff Higgins to reinforce Jeff’s wife Gretchen in Silesia.  The maelstrom in Poland grows . . . and grows . . . and grows . . .  Will it drag all its displaced Americans and their allies down with it? He’s the author/creator of the multiple New York Times best-selling Ring of Fire series starting with first novel 1632. With David Drake he has written six popular novels in the “Belisarius” alternate Roman history series, and with David Weber collaborated on 1633 and 1634: The Baltic War and latest Honorverse series entry Cauldron of Ghosts. Flint\'s latest Ring of Fire novel is 1636: The Ottoman Onslaught. Flint was for many years a labor union activist.
